# NFHS Visual Materials

**Degree Path:** Certificate in High School Basketball Officiating - NFHS Track
**Academic Level:** High School Foundation / NFHS Rules
**Course Cover:** `frontend/public/assets/images/refzone/course-covers/nfhs.svg`

## Course Overview

The NFHS track prepares high-school basketball officials to serve education-based athletics with rules accuracy, professional communication, strong mechanics, student-athlete safety, and state-association readiness.

## Course Image Brief

**Visual Elements:** education-based high-school basketball gym with a polished court, state-association rulebook, whistle, striped official shirt, coach communication card, and student-athlete safety checklist
**Visual Emphasis:** rules accuracy, student-athlete safety, sportsmanship, mechanics, and state association readiness
**Image Prompt:** Create a RefZone University course-card image for NFHS: education-based high-school basketball gym with a polished court, state-association rulebook, whistle, striped official shirt, coach communication card, and student-athlete safety checklist. Emphasize rules accuracy, student-athlete safety, sportsmanship, mechanics, and state association readiness. Use a premium basketball officiating education style with black, metallic silver, white, and orange accents, clean readable course title text, dramatic court lighting, and professional academic training energy. Avoid real school logos, real league logos, and recognizable real people.

## Graduation Requirements

- Complete all 52 weeks of daily academic work.
- Pass written NFHS rules and case-play examinations.
- Complete mechanics labs in two-person and three-person systems.
- Submit film-lab worksheets, role-play scores, mentor notes, and live-practicum evidence.
- Defend the final NFHS portfolio before the RefZone University advancement board.

## Weekly Materials

### Week 1: Orientation and Professional Identity

- Screenshot package: learner screen, week overview, active lesson view, and progress state.
- Presentation source: `docs/refzone-university/presentation-outlines/nfhs-presentation.md#week-1`.
- Required evidence: Students must produce a written journal entry, NFHS rule/case-play worksheet, mechanics-lab rubric, film note, role-play score, and mentor note showing how Orientation and Professional Identity affects high-school game administration.
- Day 1: Professor Lecture and Socratic Seminar - Professor Lecture; visual `/assets/images/refzone/lesson-visuals/lecture.svg`.
  - Screenshot: `/assets/images/refzone/course-screenshots/nfhs-lecture.svg`.
  - Required reading: Read the current NFHS Basketball Rules Book sections tied to Orientation and Professional Identity; mark definitions, penalties, exceptions, and restart language that affect Professor Lecture and Socratic Seminar. Read the current NFHS Basketball Case Book, interpretations, and state association bulletins connected to Orientation and Professional Identity; write the ruling, the reason, the crew responsibility, and the best supervisor explanation. Study the current NFHS Basketball Officials Manual, two-person and three-person mechanics, and state association mechanics directives for the day's coverage problem; draw the official's starting position, movement path, primary area, secondary awareness, and reporting route. Review education-based athletics sportsmanship, bench decorum, facility, game administration, and state association reporting procedures; identify the correct professional response when a coach, player, partner, table crew, observer, or supervisor challenges the ruling. Study the professor lecture visual aid and screenshot packet; bring one film, court, or written example that proves how the reading changes game behavior.
  - Assignment: Submit the daily journal entry, worksheet or lab artifact, and one mentor-ready evidence item for Professor Lecture and Socratic Seminar.
  - Assessment: Written Knowledge Check - 85% or mentor approval is required before Day 2 unlocks.
  - Test: NFHS Week 1, Day 1 Written Knowledge Check; passing score 85%.
  - Line Item 1 - Professor Explanation: instruction-slide; Professor-facing lecture slide, visual aid, and discussion prompt.
  - Line Item 2 - What the Student Performs: student-activity; Student-facing worksheet, lab action, and participation artifact.
  - Line Item 3 - Expected Outcome, Evidence, and Grading: assessment-evidence; Assessment-facing quiz/test item, rubric row, and evidence checkpoint.

Review education-based athletics sportsmanship, bench decorum, facility, game administration, and state association reporting procedures; identify the correct professional response when a coach, player, partner, table crew, observer, or supervisor challenges the ruling. Review education-based athletics sportsmanship, bench decorum, facility, game administration, and state association reporting procedures; identify the correct professional response when a coach, player, partner, table crew, observer, or supervisor challenges the ruling. Study the rules and case plays visual aid and screenshot packet; bring one film, court, or written example that proves how the reading changes game behavior.
  - Assignment: Submit the daily journal entry, worksheet or lab artifact, and one mentor-ready evidence item for Rules, Case Plays, and Written Reasoning.
  - Assessment: Rules Quiz - 85% or mentor approval is required before Day 3 unlocks.
  - Test: NFHS Week 21, Day 2 Rules Quiz; passing score 85%.

- Required evidence: Students must produce a written journal entry, NFHS rule/case-play worksheet, mechanics-lab rubric, film note, role-play score, and mentor note showing how Substitutions, Timeouts, Correctable Errors, and Administrative Rulings affects high-school game administration.
- Day 1: Professor Lecture and Socratic Seminar - Professor Lecture; visual `/assets/images/refzone/lesson-visuals/lecture.svg`.
  - Screenshot: `/assets/images/refzone/course-screenshots/nfhs-lecture.svg`.
  - Required reading: Read the current NFHS Basketball Rules Book sections tied to Substitutions, Timeouts, Correctable Errors, and Administrative Rulings; mark definitions, penalties, exceptions, and restart language that affect Professor Lecture and Socratic Seminar. Read the current NFHS Basketball Case Book, interpretations, and state association bulletins connected to Substitutions, Timeouts, Correctable Errors, and Administrative Rulings; write the ruling, the reason, the crew responsibility, and the best supervisor explanation. Study the current NFHS Basketball Officials Manual, two-person and three-person mechanics, and state association mechanics directives for the day's coverage problem; draw the official's starting position, movement path, primary area, secondary awareness, and reporting route. Review education-based athletics sportsmanship, bench decorum, facility, game administration, and state association reporting procedures; identify the correct professional response when a coach, player, partner, table crew, observer, or supervisor challenges the ruling. Study the professor lecture visual aid and screenshot packet; bring one film, court, or written example that proves how the reading changes game behavior.
  - Assignment: Submit the daily journal entry, worksheet or lab artifact, and one mentor-ready evidence item for Professor Lecture and Socratic Seminar.
  - Assessment: Written Knowledge Check - 85% or mentor approval is required before Day 2 unlocks.
  - Test: NFHS Week 30, Day 1 Written Knowledge Check; passing score 85%.
  - Line Item 1 - Professor Explanation: instruction-slide; Professor-facing lecture slide, visual aid, and discussion prompt.
  - Line Item 2 - What the Student Performs: student-activity; Student-facing worksheet, lab action, and participation artifact.
  - Line Item 3 - Expected Outcome, Evidence, and Grading: assessment-evidence; Assessment-facing quiz/test item, rubric row, and evidence checkpoint.

Review education-based athletics sportsmanship, bench decorum, facility, game administration, and state association reporting procedures; identify the correct professional response when a coach, player, partner, table crew, observer, or supervisor challenges the ruling. Study the rules and case plays visual aid and screenshot packet; bring one film, court, or written example that proves how the reading changes game behavior.
  - Assignment: Submit the daily journal entry, worksheet or lab artifact, and one mentor-ready evidence item for Rules, Case Plays, and Written Reasoning.
  - Assessment: Rules Quiz - 85% or mentor approval is required before Day 3 unlocks.
  - Test: NFHS Week 32, Day 2 Rules Quiz; passing score 85%.

Review education-based athletics sportsmanship, bench decorum, facility, game administration, and state association reporting procedures; identify the correct professional response when a coach, player, partner, table crew, observer, or supervisor challenges the ruling. Study the reflection and mentor review visual aid and screenshot packet; bring one film, court, or written example that proves how the reading changes game behavior.
  - Assignment: Submit the daily journal entry, worksheet or lab artifact, and one mentor-ready evidence item for Reflection, Remediation, Mentor Conference, and Advancement Record.
  - Assessment: Portfolio Evidence Check - 85% or mentor approval is required before Day 8 unlocks.
  - Test: NFHS Week 38, Day 7 Portfolio Evidence Check; passing score 85%.
  - Line Item 1 - Professor Explanation: instruction-slide; Professor-facing lecture slide, visual aid, and discussion prompt.
  - Line Item 2 - What the Student Performs: student-activity; Student-facing worksheet, lab action, and participation artifact.

Review education-based athletics sportsmanship, bench decorum, facility, game administration, and state association reporting procedures; identify the correct professional response when a coach, player, partner, table crew, observer, or supervisor challenges the ruling. Study the court mechanics lab visual aid and screenshot packet; bring one film, court, or written example that proves how the reading changes game behavior.
  - Assignment: Submit the daily journal entry, worksheet or lab artifact, and one mentor-ready evidence item for Court Laboratory and Mechanics Performance.

Review education-based athletics sportsmanship, bench decorum, facility, game administration, and state association reporting procedures; identify the correct professional response when a coach, player, partner, table crew, observer, or supervisor challenges the ruling. Study the professor lecture visual aid and screenshot packet; bring one film, court, or written example that proves how the reading changes game behavior.
  - Assignment: Submit the daily journal entry, worksheet or lab artifact, and one mentor-ready evidence item for Professor Lecture and Socratic Seminar.
  - Assessment: Written Knowledge Check - 85% or mentor approval is required before Day 2 unlocks.
  - Test: NFHS Week 50, Day 1 Written Knowledge Check; passing score 85%.

Read the current NFHS Basketball Case Book, interpretations, and state association bulletins connected to Capstone Portfolio, Advancement Board, and Season Development Plan; write the ruling, the reason, the crew responsibility, and the best supervisor explanation. Study the current NFHS Basketball Officials Manual, two-person and three-person mechanics, and state association mechanics directives for the day's coverage problem; draw the official's starting position, movement path, primary area, secondary awareness, and reporting route. Review education-based athletics sportsmanship, bench decorum, facility, game administration, and state association reporting procedures; identify the correct professional response when a coach, player, partner, table crew, observer, or supervisor challenges the ruling.
